17/01/25, 10:26â€¯pm - Shubham Verma: 2nd wlae ka Jo solution socha abhi vo already proposed hai outer ring road ke liye  ( Singapore, Netherlands )

cameras ensure that vehicles maintain a predefined minimum distance based on speed. For example:
At low speeds (30 km/h), a 5-meter distance approx
At higher speeds (60+ km/h), a larger gap (e.g., 15-20 meters) is enforced.
If a vehicle comes too close to another, the system alerts both drivers and logs a violation.

Preventing Stop-and-Go Traffic (Phantom Traffic Jams):

Enforcing consistent distances between vehicles eliminates erratic braking and acceleration.
This reduces cascading effects of abrupt stops, ensuring slowdowns instead of jams.

23/01/25, 12:19â€¯pm - ~. ROSHAN .~: class Solution {
public:
    int countServers(vector<vector<int>>& grid) {
        int m = grid.size();
        int n = grid[0].size(); 

        vector<int> rowCount(m, 0); 
        vector<int> colCount(n, 0); 

       
        for (int i = 0; i < m; i++) {
            for (int j = 0; j < n; j++) {
                if (grid[i][j] == 1) {
                    rowCount[i]++;
                    colCount[j]++;
                    
                }
            }
        }

        int result = 0;

        
        for (int i = 0; i < m; i++) {
            for (int j = 0; j < n; j++) {
                if (grid[i][j] == 1 && (rowCount[i] > 1 || colCount[j] > 1)) {
                    result++;
                }
            }
        }

        return result;
    }
};

28/01/25, 9:50â€¯pm - Shubham Verma: Certainly! To install and use DeepSeek AI on your local machine without utilizing Ollama, you can follow these steps:


---

1. Prerequisites

Ensure your system meets the following requirements:

Operating System: Windows, macOS, or Linux.

Hardware: A modern CPU; a dedicated GPU is recommended for optimal performance, especially with larger models.

Disk Space: Adequate storage for model files (ranging from a few GBs to over 40 GB, depending on the model size).



---

2. Set Up a Python Environment

DeepSeek AI is built using Python. Setting up a virtual environment ensures that dependencies are managed efficiently.

Install Python:

Download and install Python 3.8 or later from the official website.


Create a Virtual Environment:

Open your terminal or command prompt.

Navigate to your desired project directory.

Run the following commands:

python3 -m venv deepseek_env
source deepseek_env/bin/activate  # On Windows, use `deepseek_env\Scripts\activate`




---

3. Clone the DeepSeek Repository

Obtain the latest version of DeepSeek by cloning its repository.

Clone the Repository:

Run:

git clone https://github.com/DeepSeekAI/DeepSeek.git
cd DeepSeek




---

4. Install Dependencies

Install the necessary Python packages required for DeepSeek.

Install Packages:

Ensure your virtual environment is activated.

Run:

pip install -r requirements.txt




---

5. Download the DeepSeek-R1 Model

DeepSeek offers various model sizes to accommodate different hardware capabilities.

Available Models:

deepseek-r1:1.5b

deepseek-r1:7b

deepseek-r1:8b

deepseek-r1:14b

deepseek-r1:32b

deepseek-r1:70b


Choose a Model:

For beginners or those with limited hardware resources, start with the 1.5b model.

As you become more comfortable or if your hardware permits, experiment with larger models for enhanced performance.


Download the Model:

Navigate to the DeepSeek models directory:

cd models

Download the desired model using a tool like wget or curl:

wget https://deepseek.ai/models/deepseek-r1-1.5b.bin




---

6. Configure DeepSeek

Set up DeepSeek to recognize and utilize the downloaded model.

Configuration File:

Locate the config.yaml file in the DeepSeek directory.

Edit the file to point to the path of the downloaded model:

model_path: "path/to/deepseek-r1-1.5b.bin"




---

7. Run DeepSeek

Start the DeepSeek application to begin interacting with the AI model.

Launch DeepSeek:

From the DeepSeek directory, run:

python deepseek_app.py


Interact with the Model:

Once the application is running, you can input queries and receive responses from the DeepSeek AI model.




---

Note: Running larger models demands more computational resources. If you encounter performance issues, consider using a smaller model or upgrading your hardware.

By following these steps, you can successfully install and utilize DeepSeek AI on your local machine without relying on Ollama. As you become more familiar with the system, you can explore larger models and advanced configurations to suit your needs.

28/01/25, 11:39â€¯pm - ~. ROSHAN .~: class Solution {
public:
    int countNodes(TreeNode* root) {
        if(root == NULL ) return 0;
        queue<TreeNode*> q;
        int tot =1;
        q.push(root);
        
        while (!q.empty()) {
            TreeNode* node = q.front();
            q.pop();

            if (node->left) {
                tot++;
                q.push(node->left);
            }

            if (node->right) {
                tot++;
                q.push(node->right);
            }
        }

        return tot;
        
    }
};

04/02/25, 12:19â€¯am - ~. ROSHAN .~: class Solution {
public:
    int longestMonotonicSubarray(vector<int>& nums) {
        if (nums.size() <= 1) return nums.size(); 
        
        int inc = 1, dec = 1;  
        int ans = 1; 

        for (int i = 1; i < nums.size(); i++) {
            if (nums[i] > nums[i - 1]) {
                inc++;
                dec = 1;
            } 
            else if (nums[i] < nums[i - 1]) {
                dec++;
                inc = 1;
            } 
            else {
                inc = dec = 1;
            }
            ans = max(ans, max(inc, dec));
        }

        return ans;
    }
};

04/02/25, 7:08â€¯pm - ~. ROSHAN .~: class Solution {
public:
    int maxAscendingSum(vector<int>& nums) {

        int start = nums[0];
        int sum = nums[0]; 
        for (int i = 1 ; i < nums.size(); i++){
            if(nums[i] > nums[i-1]){
                start +=  nums[i];
            }
            else{
                start = nums[i];
            }

            sum = max ( sum , start );
        }

        return sum ; 
        
    }
};

05/02/25, 10:34â€¯pm - ~. ROSHAN .~: class Solution {
public:
    bool areAlmostEqual(string s1, string s2) {
        
        int count = 0  ; 
        int first = 0 ; 
        int second = 0 ; 
        for(int i = 0 ; i < s1.size() ; i++){
            if(s1[i] != s2[i]){
                count++;
                if(count == 1){
                    first = i ;
                }
                else if(count == 2) second = i;

                if(count > 2 ) return false ; 
            }

        }
        if(!count) return true; 

        if(!count%2) return false ; 

        if(s1[first] == s2[second] && s1[second] == s2[first]) return true ; 

        return false ; 
        
    }
};

06/02/25, 8:50â€¯pm - ~. ROSHAN .~: https://leetcode.com/problems/number-of-great-partitions/description/
06/02/25, 8:50â€¯pm - Shubham Verma: Constant
07/02/25, 12:01â€¯am - ~. ROSHAN .~: class Solution {
public:
    int tupleSameProduct(vector<int>& nums) {
        unordered_map<int, int> mp;
        int ans = 0, n = nums.size();
        for (int i = 0; i < n; i++)
            for (int j = i + 1; j < n; j++) {
                int product = nums[i] * nums[j];
                ans += 8 * mp[product];
                mp[product]++;
            }
        return ans;
    }
};

03/03/25, 8:28â€¯pm - ~. ROSHAN .~: ### A. Does the given graph contain a deadlock? Justification:

To determine if the graph contains a deadlock, we need to check for a **circular wait** condition, which is one of the necessary conditions for a deadlock. A circular wait occurs when there is a cycle in the Resource Allocation Graph (RAG).

#### Observations:
1. **Processes and Resources:**
   - Processes: P1, P2, P3, P4
   - Resources: R1, R2, R3, R4
2. **Edges:**
   - A directed edge from a process to a resource (e.g., P1 â†’ R1) indicates that the process is requesting the resource.
   - A directed edge from a resource to a process (e.g., R1 â†’ P2) indicates that the resource is allocated to the process.

#### Cycle Detection:
- From the graph:
  - P1 â†’ R1 â†’ P2 â†’ R3 â†’ P3 â†’ R4 â†’ P4 â†’ R2 â†’ P1
  - This forms a **cycle**, indicating that all processes and resources are involved in a circular wait condition.

**Conclusion:** Yes, the graph contains a deadlock because there is a cycle in the Resource Allocation Graph.

---

### B. How can the circular wait condition be broken to prevent deadlocks?

To prevent deadlocks, one of the necessary conditions (mutual exclusion, hold and wait, no preemption, or circular wait) must be eliminated. Breaking the **circular wait condition** can be achieved by imposing an **ordering on resources**.

#### Solution: Assign a Global Resource Ordering
- Assign a unique number to each resource (e.g., R1 = 1, R2 = 2, R3 = 3, R4 = 4).
- Enforce that processes must request resources in an increasing order of their numbers.
- For example:
  - If P1 needs both R1 and R3, it must first request R1 (lower number) and then request R3 (higher number).

#### Example:
- Suppose:
  - P1 requests R1 first and then requests R3.
  - P2 requests R3 first and then requests R4.
- With resource ordering enforced:
  - If P2 wants to request R4 after holding R3, it cannot do so unless it releases all lower-numbered resources (e.g., R3). This prevents circular waiting.

**Conclusion:** By enforcing an ordering on resource allocation requests, circular wait conditions can be avoided, thereby preventing deadlocks.
